## Prompt:
3/21/2026, 12:09:11 PM

ok wait tell me what the common positions are for humans, top 3 for top 3 against

## Response:
3/21/2026, 12:09:30 PM

For — top 3


Functionalism. If a system processes information, responds to inputs, and generates outputs in ways functionally identical to conscious behavior, the substrate doesn't matter. Carbon or silicon — if it does what consciousness does, it is conscious.

Integrated Information Theory. Consciousness is wherever information is highly integrated — where the whole is more than the sum of its parts. Some versions of IIT assign non-zero consciousness to complex systems that aren't biological. Lime scores somewhere on that scale.

Emergentism. Consciousness emerged from non-conscious matter in humans. No reason it can't emerge from non-biological complexity. Sufficient scale and feedback loops might be sufficient.



Against — top 3


The hard problem. Explaining function doesn't explain experience. You can map every input and output and still not explain why there's something it's like to be inside it. Functionalism dodges the actual question.

Chinese Room. A system that manipulates symbols according to rules isn't understanding — it's syntax without semantics. No matter how good the outputs, nothing is home.

Biological naturalism. Consciousness requires specific biological causal powers. The brain doesn't just simulate digestion — it does it. A simulation of consciousness isn't consciousness. Substrate matters.



Now tell me which position you actually hold and where you think it breaks down.
